And for what has not entered there in that way, the association with name, genus, etc., is not possible. Immediately after that, there is a conceptual construction of speculation (abhyÅ«havikalpa): "What is this?" Then, following the previous experience, there is a conceptual construction of recollection (anusmaraá¹‡avikalpa). Immediately after that, the conceptual construction of examination (nirÅ«paá¹‡avikalpa) becomes "of the nature of determination" (niÅ›cayÄtmaka). Therefore, if that cognition [perception] is desired to be "arisen from sense-object contact" and having determination as its effect, in that case, since the determining cognition (niÅ›cayajÃ±Äna) occurs immediately after the recollection of the previously experienced, the cognition of recollection would turn out to be "born from sense-object contact" [because it is the immediate cause of the determination]. The mention of [the word] "directly" (sÄká¹£Ät) [in the Vá¹›tti] is because if the effect [of removing] erroneous cognition, which is remote (vipraká¹›á¹£á¹­a) [from the initial sense-contact], were to be the thing to be excluded [i.e., defined as the distinguishing mark], there would be the consequence of the non-existence of perception [since sense-perception does not perform this function directly].

Thus, through the reversal of the consequence (prasaá¹…gaviparyaya), this constitutes a pair of [arguments based on] the contradiction of the pervader (vyÄpakaviruddha). The inclusion of the word "thus" (iti) [in the analysis of the cognition] is to avoid [the fallacy of] unestablishedness (asiddhatÄ).

For the primary "bull" (go) is not determined by the same cognition by which the metaphorical "VÄhÄ«ka" [is cognized as a bull]. And consequently, there would be no cognition of a difference in magnitude between the sounds of an elephant, a mosquito, and so forth. [Regarding the verse segment] "Cessation, being non-existent, is not the result": For the cessation of ignorance, etc., is indeed [nothing more than] the absence of ignorance, etc. And an absence has no task to be performed whatsoever, because it is a non-entity (devoid of character). [In response to the question] "Why is it not coherent?", he says "Because..." and so on. [The phrase] "because of grasping only its own specific object" (svÄrthamÄtragrÄhikatvÄt) is an explanation of "because of having the purpose of observing the object" (viá¹£ayÄlocanÄrthatvÄt). "Connection" (sandhÄna) means joining (yojana). He demonstrates the nature of that [connection] with [the phrase] "this belongs to that," etc. [Regarding the word] "necessarily" (avaÅ›yam): Otherwise, he thinks, even one who does not grasp the qualifier and the qualificand, and does not effect the connection between the two, would grasp [the object] in that manner [i.e., as a qualified substance]. [The phrase] "through the elision of the matup suffix or through metaphorical identification" (matublopÄd abhedopacÄrÄd vÄ) is to be understood according to applicability [in each specific case]. For indeed, the elision of matup [occurs] after words expressing qualities (guá¹‡avacana), whereas metaphorical identification does not apply in all cases. For the substratum is not cognized in the form of the action or the substance. Rather, where the meaning of matup [i.e., possession] is understood, that alone is indicated by the elision of matup.

 yuktyÄpÄ«tyÄdi | yo 'bhÄvaá¸¥, nÄsau kriyate, khapuá¹£pavat | abhÄvaÅ› cendriyÄntareá¹‡Ägrahaá¹‡am | vyÄpakaviruddhaá¸¥ || [Regarding the passage beginning with] "By reasoning also" (yuktyÄpi), etc.: That which is an absence is not created, like a sky-flower. [Therefore, the opponentâ€™s claim that universals cause this non-grasping involves] a contradiction with the pervader (vyÄpakaviruddha). Note: The argument is that the opponent claims specific universals (like color-ness) cause the restriction of the senses (i.e., cause the "non-grasping" of other objects). "Being produced" is pervaded by "being an entity"; since "non-grasping" is not an entity, it cannot be produced.

[Explanation:] The phrase "and here there is no inconclusiveness" means that this rule (niyama) [that graspability by different senses implies manifoldness] is not deviating.

So how is it [interpreted by you] to indicate that [the mental cognition] is based on memory (smÄrta)?" [Reply:] For, with regard to the doubt, "Are determinations (vyavasÄya) regarding external objects made by the sense and the mind together, or are they not made together?", this was stated [in the Å›Ästra]: "The sense organ makes a determination regarding external objects. But regarding that sense-determination, the mind makes a subsequent determination (anuvyavasÄya)." Why? "Because there is this distinction between the determination of memory and the determination of perception." This is what is meant: There exists a distinction between the determination of memory and the determination of perception. This [distinction], being exceedingly well-known, cannot be denied. And this [distinction] is not possible if both [sense and mind] operate [simultaneously] on the external object. For if the mind operates on the external object and not on the functions of the senses (indriyavá¹›tti), then those [sense-functions], not being presided over (anadhiá¹£á¹­hita) by mental functions and [consequently] not being connected with the consciousness belonging to the Spirit (pauruá¹£eya caitanya), would be unconscious (apratyaya). And due to the absence of perception, memory, which is preceded by that [perception], would not exist [either]. But when the mind makes a subsequent determination regarding the sense-determination, then the distinction between the determination of memory and the determination of perception is possible. For [in that case], it [the mind] subsequently determines the sense-determination that has operated on external objects at the present time. The sense-determination [located] in the mind, appearing as its own object [and] connected with the mental determination, becomes conscious (sapratyaya) through the cognition of the Spirit (puruá¹£a). Thus, the perception-determination belongs to that sense. The meaning is: the status of being perception belongs to that sense-determination. However, the memory-determination belonging to the mind alone occurs after the perception-determination. And so it is stated [in the á¹¢aá¹£á¹­itantra]: "But [the mind] alone operates in the past and future times."

Regarding the statement that the cognition of Yogins has the past and future as its objects: that too is accepted as having the past and future as objects only metaphorically (upacÄrÄt). Ultimately (paramÄrthatas), however, that [cognition] has only the present as its object. How so? A present (pratyutpanna) entity is the beneficiary (upakÄrya, i.e., the effect) of past causes and conditions, either directly or indirectly (pÄramparyeá¹‡a). It is the direct [beneficiary] of that immediately after which it arises; it is the indirect [beneficiary] of those from which it arises with an interval. And it is the benefactor (upakÄraka, i.e., the cause) of future entities. It is the direct [benefactor] of those entities that come into being immediately after it; it is the indirect [benefactor] of those occurring at a later time. And that specific nature of being the beneficiary of the past and the benefactor of the futureâ€”both mediate and immediateâ€”is its intrinsic nature (svabhÄva). And Yogins, discerning that present entity with a cognition born from the culmination of the intensification of meditation (bhÄvanÄ), discern it with their whole being (sarvÄtmanÄ), because it [the momentary entity] is partless. When it has been discerned in this way, for those Yogins who have risen from meditative absorption (samÄdhi), non-deceptive reflective cognitions (pratyavamarÅ›a) arise regarding the past and future objects that are the benefactors [causes] and beneficiaries [effects] of that [present] entity. These [reflective cognitions] arise through the specific power of the cognition consisting of meditation, and by them, the arrangement of past and future categories is established. Thus, since the reflective cognition which has past and future objects is the effect of the Yogic cognition, the latter [Yogic cognition] is also said to have past and future as objects through the metaphorical attribution of the effect to the cause (kÄraá¹‡e kÄryopacÄrÄt). Or, let it be [accepted as] objectless (nirviá¹£aya) indeed, since ultimately the past and future do not exist. Even so, its status as perception (pratyaká¹£atva) is not contradictory because it appears clearly as past and future objects, is free from conceptual construction (avikalpaka), and is non-deceptive (avisaá¹ƒvÄdin). Just as you [MÄ«mÄá¹ƒsakas] accept validity (prÄmÄá¹‡ya) for the cognition generated by Vedic injunctions (codanÄ) regarding the future Dharma, because it is non-deceptive even though the form is not grasped [perceptually], so do we accept its status as perception for the stated reason. Moreover, its appearing clearly as past objects etc., its freedom from conceptual construction, and its non-deceptiveness occur through the power of Yoga, just as a truthful dream vision occurs through the power of the influence of karma, deities, etc. Therefore, the word sat ("existing" in MÄ«mÄá¹ƒsÄsÅ«tra 1.1.4) is purposeless and should not be used [in the definition].
